======================================================================
PAGE: Shard
CATEGORIES: Bonehunters
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Shard
======================================================================

"
Clever beats nasty every time.
"
―Shard
Shard
was originally a soldier in the 5th squad,
2nd Company of the
Ashok Regiment
. He was a corporal in
Sergeant
Cord
's squad.
He was a half-brother of
Sinn
and described as a young man.
In
House of Chains
Shard was stationed with the Ashok Regiment under Captain
Kindly
in
Silver Lake
on
Genabackis
.  He, Cord, and others in their squad were under house arrest for drunkeness when
Karsa Orlong
attacked their garrison.  The
mage
,
Ebron
, armed Shard and the other squad members and they were able to capture the rampaging
Teblor
.  Shard recommended they kill the warrior who had slain many of their fellows.
Shard was amongst those under siege in the ancient cliff-side fortress of
B'ridys
by
Irriz
and his
Seven Cities
renegades. From his reaction, probably unbeknown to Shard, his half-sister
Sinn
was outside the fortress. She and the recently arrived
Kalam Mekhar
both pretended to Irriz that they would help him however secretly took steps to help those inside the fortress. When they made contact with the besieged, Kalam gave Sinn into their care whilst wiping out the renegades with the help of an
Azalan
demon. Upon entering the fortress, Kalam observed Sinn with her arms wrapped around her half-brother. Cord had been in charge since Kindly and Pores had disappeared and now put Kalam in charge of his old squad, with seniority over Shard.
This arrangement did not last long as the
Bridgeburner
pulled rank on Cord.
Kalam suggested the regiment leave B'ridys and join
Adjunct
Tavore Paran
's
Malaz 14th Army
, which was marching toward
Raraku
.  In the aftermath of the
Battle of Raraku
, the regiment's 16 survivors ambushed and slew the sorceress,
Fayelle
, and a small band of
Dogslayers
.  Shard pulled Sinn up into his saddle behind him as they fled the onrushing waters that flooded Raraku.
In
The Bonehunters
After the Battle of Raraku, the Ashok Regiment was incorporated into the 9th Company of the
8th Legion
within the 14th Army.  Cord's 5th squad remained intact although it was redesignated as the 7th squad.
Leoman
led the
Army of the Apocalypse
westward to
Y'Ghatan
and the 14th Army followed. Adjunct Tavore launched the
Last Siege of Y'Ghatan
by sending the army's
sappers
to breach the city's wall under the cover of night.  First into the city were the Malazan
marines
, followed quickly by the
Heavy infantry
.
Fist
Keneb
then ordered Cord to lead the 9th Company's seventh through twelfth
medium infantry
squads into Y'Ghatan.
Once inside the city, the Malazans immediately came under heavy attack by hidden swordsmen and archers. Cord's squad linked up with
Mosel
's heavy infantry following
Fiddler
's marines. Cord first thought to send Shard back to Keneb to relay Fiddler's advice recommending leading their advance with sappers, but chose Sinn instead.
When enough Malazans were engaged in street fighting inside the city, Leoman sprung his trap. The city's olive oil-soaked buildings were set alight and the streets quickly became an inferno. Cord's squad fled the flames along with a mixed group of survivors from
Sobelone
's,
Balm
's, Fiddler's,
Hellian
's, and
Gesler
's squads  True to his name, Limp broke his left leg during the fighting when it became trapped under a sliding piece of stonework. Shard, Cord, and other members of the Ashok Regiment had to pull him free.
Shard was among the small group of soldiers who survived Y'Ghatan by tunneling their way out from under the city. They spent three days crawling on their hands and knees through the dark led by
Bottle
and his
rat
. Like many others, Shard found the experience so claustrophobic and frightening that he began gibbering in terror. When Limp began screaming in front of him, Shard pounded his squad mate's head against the ground until Limp lost consciousness to shut him up.
Koryk
grew concerned over the unmoving Limp, so Shard twisted the soldier's broken leg to immediately rouse him and show he still lived.
Unaware that any had survived, the 14th Army made haste for the
Kokakal Sea
to embark on
Admiral
Nok
's ships and escape the
Bluetongue Plague
ravaging Seven Cities. Sinn was still outside the city when it burned and did not accept that her half-brother was lost. She deserted the army, bringing
Faradan Sort
along, in order to find the spot where Shard and the others struggled to crawl the final feet to open air. Sinn wrapped herself in his arms while he sat in shock with staring, unseeing eyes.
Shard and the others made the long march west, finally catching up to the army on the coast.
Aboard one of Nok's ships, Shard worried about his sister. She would not tell him what had happened to her at their former estate. He kept an eye on her as she intimately crawled under the cloaks of several soldiers, fearing that someone might take advantage of her, and was grateful when no one did. After the experience of Y'Ghatan, he said he and his fellows no longer belonged to the Ashok Regiment—they were Bonehunters.
Nok's fleet returned to
Malaz City
where the Adjunct met with Empress
Laseen
.
In
Reaper's Gale
Adjunct Tavore clashed with Empress Laseen at Malaz City and took the
Bonehunters
rogue, following the
Tiste Edur
fleet
that had ravaged
Sepik
back to
Lether
to invade the
Letherii Empire
.
Cord and Balm's squads took the
Silanda
to the island of
Second Maiden Fort
off the coast of Lether to establish a headquarters and resupply base for the Adjunct.
They found the island on the verge of being destroyed under a mountain of ice released by the collapse of
Gothos
' ancient
Omtose Phellack
ritual, but Sinn was able to hold the ice back with her magic until its force was spent. The island's self-declared ruler,
Brullyg
, gratefully welcomed the Malazans as royal guests until they placed him under house arrest and secretly took control of the island.
Shard, Crump and Sinn by
Shadaan
While Balm's squad kept Brullyg under guard and monitored the island from its only town, Cord's squad patrolled the island's coast and interior while awaiting Tavore's arrival.
Shard was sick with worry over his sister, who had stopped speaking to anyone including himself. The giggling girl he once carried over his shoulders was gone since Y'Ghatan and it frightened him. Now she was a child witch, a
High Mage
with a thirst for blood, and a Child of
Dryjhna
the Apocalyptic.
While on patrol,
Crump
's endless mad songs grated on Shard's nerves.
Shard also placed a bet of five
imperials
on Limp experiencing one of his characteristic injuries within the month. Limp was disgusted when Shard reasoned that he was about due.
Meanwhile Tavore sent Fist Keneb's marines to the mainland, spreading them in isolated pairs of squads across thirty leagues of coast and burning their
transport vessels
behind them. The marines moved forward into the
Letherii
countryside towards
Letheras
, the capital, with orders to kill Edur by night and stir the occupied Letherii into rebellion. Each squad had a mage responsible for hiding their presence and confusing their enemies.
Shurq Elalle
and her ship,
Undying Gratitude
, were caught up in the Malazan blockade of Second Maiden Fort's port. When Adjunct Tavore arrived with the rest of the Malazan fleet, she hired the pirate to guide them to the mouth of the
Lether River
leading to Letheras.
Cord and Balm's squads made the journey on the
Silanda
.
The Adjunct's fleet made landfall near Letheras and defeated the city's
Imperial Brigade
.
Meanwhile, Keneb's marines secretly entered the city to secure its western gate to allow the rest of the army entrance.
Soon the City Garrison surrendered and the city fell.
In
Dust of Dreams
(Information needed)
In
The Crippled God
(Information needed)

Shipwreck
was a regular in the
Bonehunters
. He would stagger drunkenly in moments of high excitement as his damaged inner ear would start acting up.
In
The Crippled God
He was part of a group of regulars who rushed out to defend
Adjunct
Tavore
's position in the battle against the
Forkrul Assail
.
Shipwreck was detailed by
Corporal
Grid Ffan
to join him,
Could Howl
, and

======================================================================
PAGE: Shoaly
CATEGORIES: Bonehunters
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Shoaly
======================================================================

Shoaly
was a
heavy
in
Sergeant
Sinter
's
4th Squad
,
8th Legion, 3rd Company
of the
Bonehunters
. He had the red hair and blue eyes common to the
Falari
people, but also the olive-hued skin of the
Falari Isles
' indigenous
Walk
population.
He was fond of
Flashwit
.
The soldiers of the Bonehunters thought of him and fellow heavies,
Drawfirst
and
Lookback
, as cousins because of their similar appearance and heritage, but none of the three knew each other before enlisting.
In
Reaper's Gale
Adjunct
Tavore Paran
clashed with Empress
Laseen
at
Malaz City
and took the Bonehunters rogue, following the
Tiste Edur
fleet
that had ravaged
Sepik
back to
Lether
.
Tavore invaded the
Letherii Empire
, burning her
transport
vessels on the shoreline and spreading the
marines
in isolated pairs of squads across thirty leagues of coast. The marines moved forward into the
Letherii
countryside towards
Letheras
, the capital, with orders to kill Edur by night and stir the occupied Letherii into rebellion. Each squad had a mage responsible for hiding their presence and confusing their enemies.
Sinter's squad, along with
Badan Gruk
's 5th and
Primly
's 10th squads, landed furthest south of all the marines. Remaining together, they saw little resistance moving east and soon reached a river. Rather than slog through through waist-deep swamp muck, they stole a fisher boat and sailed upriver. They made excellent time until running into a Letherii galley in the night.
Kisswhere
and Sinter were lost in the water during a discharge of
Moranth munitions
. Forced ashore, they were pursued day and night, using up their mages dodging and ducking enemy attacks.
Corporal
Pravalak Rim
led the 4th squad in Sinter's place, while Lookback took point with Shoaly and Drawfirst covering the group's rear.
Contrary to the Adjunct's expectations, the Letherii soldiers did not use the
Malazan
invasion to turn against their Edur occupiers.
The marines further north saw intense action, and as they neared Letheras fighting became more desperate and their munition supplies dwindled.
Hellian
and
Urb
's squads earned the support of the Letherii slave and
Indebted
classes by changing tactics to slay the government officials, lawyers, and debt-holders in each village.
Fiddler
and
Gesler
's squads joined them at a tavern a day's travel from the capital just in time for a force of hundreds of Edur to envelop the village the Malazans occupied.
Three days after leaving the river, Sinter, Primly, and Badan Gruk's squads came upon the overwhelmed Malazans and turned the tide of battle with their fresh supply of munitions. The new arrivals deferred to Fiddler's seniority, and the former
Bridgeburner
ordered the marines to hold their position in hopes they would be reinforced by
Fist
Keneb
.
Noting Gesler and
Stormy
among the village's marines, Lookback argued with Shoaly and Drawfirst over whether the pair should be killed for betraying the
Cult of the Boar
. Shoaly argued that Gesler and Stormy were not to blame for the cult being outlawed and asked Drawfirst to "explain it to this fool." Drawfirst said they were all going to die in the coming engagement and Lookback had the choice of dying with his fellow heavies or dying alone. If she saw him creeping up on Gesler or Stormy she would lop his head off herself.
By the time Keneb's forces arrived, thousands of Edur followed in their wake, pushing the gathered Malazans towards the city where the
Imperial Brigade
awaited.
Caught between the two armies near
Kravos Hill
, the 800 remaining Malazans
were forced to huddle under
Beak
's protective spell when the Letherii mages cast a deadly
ritual
of
Chaos
upon them and the Edur. The spell was broken, but the hair of all those under Beak's protection turned white. The Edur abandoned the field after their allies' betrayal, and the shaken Imperial Brigade withdrew to meet Adjunct Tavore's more threatening main force as it disembarked from the
Lether River
.
Keneb marched on Letheras thinking the marines deserved to be the first to enter the capital.
After the marines found a hidden entrance beneath the wall, the seized the city's western gate to allow the rest of the army entrance.
Soon the City Garrison surrendered and the city fell.
In
Dust of Dreams
(Information needed)
In
The Crippled God
It was revealed that Shoaly died earlier, presumably in the battle against the
K'Chain Nah'ruk
.

======================================================================
PAGE: Shortnose
CATEGORIES: Bonehunters
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Shortnose
======================================================================

"
He'll do anything to spite his face.
"
―Reem, on Shortnose
Shortnose
was a mean-looking
heavy
in the 9th Company,
8th Legion
of the
Malaz 14th Army
. He was in either
Sobelone
's or
Tugg
's squad.
The tip of his nose had been cut off at some point in the past, presumably the reason for his name.
He was prone to snoring very loudly.
He had huge hands.
In
House of Chains
Shortnose's squad was part of
Adjunct
Tavore Paran
's punitive expedition against the
Army of the Apocalypse
. On the road from
Aren
to
Raraku
, the heavies had no chance to wet their swords, but Fiddler was impressed with their discipline nonetheless.
In
The Bonehunters
After the
Battle of Raraku
,
Leoman
led the
Army of the Apocalypse
westward to
Y'Ghatan
and the 14th Army followed. Shortnose married fellow soldier,
Hanno
, about one week before reaching the city.  According to
Corporal
Reem
, it "aint his face she adores, if you know what I mean."
Once the 14th Army reached the city's outskirts, an impromptu wrestling match broke out between Shortnose and
Saltlick
after Saltlick bit Shortnose's ear off. The rest of Sobelone and Tugg's squads gathered around the two straining men, watching and placing bets. Hanno bet against her husband.
Adjunct Tavore launched the
Last Siege of Y'Ghatan
by sending the army's
sappers
to breach the city's wall under the cover of night. First into the city were the Malazan
marines
, followed quickly by the heavy and
medium infantry
. Once inside the city, the Malazans immediately came under attack from swordsmen on the ground and archers in the buildings above them. When enough Malazans were engaged in street fighting inside the city, Leoman sprung his trap. The city's olive oil-soaked buildings were set alight and the streets quickly became an inferno. Sobelone and Tugg were killed in the fighting and Shortnose joined a mixed group of survivors from
Cord
's,
Fiddler
's, and
Borduke
's squads. They fled the flames while Shortnose,
Flashwit
,
Mayfly
, and
Uru Hela
— armed only with knives and fists — defended the group against a score of fanatics.
Shortnose was among the small group of soldiers who survived Y'Ghatan by tunneling their way out from under the city.  They spent three days crawling on their hands and knees through the dark led by
Bottle
and his
rat
.
Unaware that any had survived, the 14th Army made haste for the
Kokakal Sea
to embark on
Admiral
Nok
's ships and escape the
Bluetongue Plague
ravaging
Seven Cities
.
Faradan Sort
and
Sinn
remained behind and discovered the survivors as they crawled from the wreckage.
Captain
Sort reorganised the shattered soldiers, placing Shortnose into
Gesler
's squad.
After the survivors rejoined the 14th Army on the coast of the
Kokakal Sea
, Gesler and
Stormy
were given back command of the
Silanda
. Shortnose served aboard the vessel along with
Balm
and Fiddler's squads on the return voyage to
Quon Tali
.
Some festering argument between Shortnose and Flashwit led to the two wrestling on the deck, growling and biting like a pair of dogs.
The Adunct's fleet travelled to
Malaz City
where Empress
Laseen
awaited Tavore in
Mock's Hold
. The
Silanda
joined Tavore's flagship, the
Froth Wolf
, to moor at the city pier while the rest of the fleet remained anchored in the harbour. The entire city seethed with magically induced anger against the 14th Army and the soldiers of the
Silanda
prepared to defend their ship from the mob after the Adjunct was escorted away.  Shortnose, Uru Hela,
Tarr
,
Corabb Bhilan Thenu'alas
, Mayfly, and Flashwit formed a shield wall that took the brunt of the mob's attack. Eventually, Shortnose was crippled by a sword through a thigh. The wound was seen to by
Deadsmell
, while
Lobe
and
Galt
stepped in to shore up the gap.
In
Reaper's Gale
Adjunct Tavore clashed with Empress Laseen at Malaz City and took the
Bonehunters
rogue, following the
Tiste Edur
fleet
that had ravaged
Sepik
back to
Lether
.
Tavore invaded the
Letherii Empire
, burning her
transport
vessels on the shoreline and spreading the marines in isolated pairs of squads across thirty leagues of coast. The marines moved forward into the Letherii countryside with orders to kill Edur by night and stir the occupied Letherii into rebellion. Each squad had a
mage
responsible for hiding their presence and confusing their enemies.
By this time, Shortnose was assigned to Gesler and Stormy's squad.
Stormy was happily impressed by the effectiveness of Shortnose and the three "dread ladies" (Flashwit, Mayfly, and Uru Hela) under his command.
But he was less impressed by Shortnose's snoring while on campaign. When repeated kicking did shut the heavy up, Stormy purposely trod on one of Shortnose's hands, breaking the third finger. When Shortnose awoke, he just looked at it, reset it, and carried on as if nothing had happened.
Gesler and Fiddler's squads remained together and at first had no problem remaining hidden from enemy soldiers.
But the Letherii soon became aware of the enemy operating in their territory. Only
Corabb
's impossible luck saved them from a clever ambush in the forest when he accidentally flushed out a deer that immediately fell with twenty arrows in it. Shortnose joined Stormy and the other heavies in breaking one side of the ambush, while the other Malazans fired crossbows and sharpers at the enemy. The Malazans quickly turned the attack until the Letherii unveiled their sorcery of grey chaotic fire, killing
Sands
. Fiddler fired a cusser into the trees above the Letherii mage killing him and shredding a score of enemy soldiers before the Malazans were forced to retreat.
Gesler and Fiddler stopped their squads at an isolated farmhouse to lay a trap for a troop of mounted pursuers. While Fiddler and
Cuttle
assembled
The Drum
out of
munitions
, Gesler sent Uru Hela to investigate the occupants of the nearby farmhouse. When the heavy was only fifteen paces from the front door, an enormous
Kenryll'ah demon prince
burst out of the house to kill her with a two-handed wood-axe. Shortnose and the other heavies flanked Stormy as they charged the demon, chopping it with their swords before Gesler called the retreat. When Gesler purposefully called out the wrong direction of retreat to confuse their potential pursuers, Stormy had to physically reign Shortnose in to prevent him from falling for the misdirection.
Ironically, the demon and its fellow prince had taken up residence in the farmhouse to retire in peace. They had just wanted to be left alone and the encounter was a tragic accident.
Contrary to the Adjunct's expectations, the Letherii soldiers did not use the Malazan invasion to turn against their Edur occupiers.
As the marines neared Letheras fighting became more desperate and Gesler and Fiddler's squads became separated.
A day's travel from the capital, Gesler's squad stumbled upon a village occupied by
Hellian
and
Urb
's squad and a number of others. Gesler and Fiddler's squad reunited at the local tavern just in time for a force of hundreds of Edur to envelop the village.
The Edur were repelled by the arrival of
Badan Gruk
,
Sinter
, and
Primly
's fresh squads.
The new arrivals deferred to Fiddler's seniority, and the former
Bridgeburner
ordered the marines to hold their position in hopes they would be reinforced by Fist Keneb.
By the time Keneb's forces arrived, thousands of Edur followed in their wake, pushing the gathered Malazans towards the city where the
Imperial Brigade
awaited.
Caught between the two armies near
Kravos Hill
, the 800 remaining Malazans
were forced to huddle under
Beak
's protective spell when the Letherii mages cast a deadly
ritual
of
Chaos
upon them and the Edur. The spell was broken, but the hair of all those under Beak's protection turned white. The Edur abandoned the field after their allies' betrayal, and the shaken Imperial Brigade withdrew to meet Adjunct Tavore's more threatening main force as it disembarked from the
Lether River
.
Keneb marched on Letheras thinking the marines deserved to be the first to enter the capital.
After the marines found a hidden entrance beneath the wall, Gesler, Fiddler,
Urb
, and Hellian's squads were sent into the city to cause trouble while the remaining marines opened the city's west gate to Tavore's infantry. Gesler's squad soon became separated from Fiddler's after the two squads teamed to ambush an assembly of the city's Main Garrison.
After the main force of Malazans entered the city, the City Garrison surrendered and the city fell.
Shortnose's wife, Hanno, died early in the invasion, her skull cleaved by a Letherii sword, while serving in Urb's squad.
In
Dust of Dreams
He had been part of Gesler's squad. After the Sergeant and Corporal Stormy were kidnapped, the squad was disbanded by
Fist
Keneb
. Given first choice, Sergeant Fiddler chose Shortnose to join his squad.
In
The Crippled God
Shortnose was described as having a long beard, decorated with the bones of fallen enemies. He had lost the four fingers of his shield hand in the battle with the
K'Chain Nah'ruk
. As the other members of the 4th squad were either dead or dispersed, Shortnose decided to join the 5th squad. No mention was made of whether he was aware of Fiddler having also chosen him.
It was revealed that Shortnose had fathered a child with his older brother's wife
Karas
in a drunken encounter.  He sent a portion of his pay home to support the child and hoped his brother would remove the bounty once the child was old enough to work.
While the Bonehunters were crossing the
Glass Desert
, Shortnose was one of the heavies tasked with helping to pull an ox cart filled with supplies.
After
Shorthand
(an ex-heavy, aka
Himble Thrup
) was viciously assaulted (in order to get him out of the way) by three goons from the regular infantry who had been picked by
Fist
Blistig
to help him recover what he thought of as 'his' secret stash of water,
Shortnose, leading a group of other heavies to avenge Shorthand, searched for and found Blistig's 'gang of thugs' (some nine or ten well-known trouble-makers) and badly mauled them - leaving them all with assorted broken bones, smashed heads and faces beaten to a pulp.

CATEGORIES: Bonehunters, Humans

Sinn
Biographical information
Race
Human
Gender
Female
Family
Shard
(half-brother)
Social information
Affiliation
Malaz 14th Army
Bonehunters
Occupation(s)
Mage
Warren(s)
Telas
Sinn
was a young
mage
of
Malazan
descent living in
Seven Cities
. She was described as a "young, slight and pallid" woman with light brown eyes.
She had a half-brother,
Shard
, who was a member of the
Ashok Regiment
.
When she was younger Sinn had had a
Tanno tutor
, who was a
Spiritwalker
.
Later, she studied magic for a time with
Fayelle
(unpleasantly) while her half-brother was posted with his regiment in
Genabackis
.  Before joining the
Whirlwind
rebellion, Fayelle had murdered Sinn's parents and attempted to kill the young mage as well.  Sinn swore revenge.
Sinn described her talents as minor magicks.
Lieutenant
Pores
thought her a "scary creature".
In
House of Chains
Sinn by
Mrakobulka
The Ashok Regiment was trapped in the cliffside fortress of
B'ridys
by a group of Seven Cities' rebels led by
Irriz
. Sinn pretended to help the rebels but sabotaged their equipment and attempted to kill them, hoping to free her half-brother. With the help of
Kalam Mekhar
, Sinn joined Shard in the fortress.
On Kalam's advice, together with the other remaining members of the Ashok Regiment, they headed towards
Raraku
. In the aftermath of the
Battle of Raraku
, Sinn and the surviving 16 members of the Ashok Regiment ambushed Fayelle and a small band of
Dogslayers
fleeing the Whirlwind camp. Fayelle became pinned under her horse where Sinn found her and cut her throat.  Fayelle died claiming she would await her old student at
Hood
's Gate and the wait would not be long. Sinn and the Ashok Regiment were immediately forced to flee as a wall of water flooded Raraku.
In
The Bonehunters
After the Battle of Raraku, the Ashok Regiment was incorporated into the 9th Company of the
8th Legion
within the 14th Army. Cord's 5th squad remained intact, although it was redesignated as the 7th squad, and Sinn officially became a member.
Leoman
led the
Army of the Apocalypse
westward to
Y'Ghatan
and the 14th Army followed.
Adjunct
Tavore Paran
launched the
Last Siege of Y'Ghatan
by sending the army's
sappers
to breach the city's wall under the cover of night. First into the city were the Malazan
marines
, followed quickly by the
Heavy infantry
.
Fist
Keneb
then ordered Cord to lead the 9th Company's seventh through twelfth
medium infantry
squads into Y'Ghatan.
Once inside the city, the Malazans immediately came under heavy attack by hidden swordsmen and archers. Cord's squad linked up with
Mosel
's heavy infantry following
Fiddler
's marines. After observing Sinn collecting fingers from the dead, Cord ended her role in the battle by forcing her to carry a message back to Keneb.
Sinn at Y'Ghatan by
Noah Bradley (Official image)
When enough Malazans were engaged in street fighting inside the city, Leoman sprung his trap. The city's olive oil-soaked buildings were set alight and the streets quickly became an inferno. Fists Keneb and
Tene Baralta
were trapped just inside the walls of the city along with nearly 800 Malazan soldiers.
Captain
Faradan Sort
spotted Sinn stumbling towards them, flames dancing in her hair and her body shedding charred leathers. But all around her the flames died in swirling darkness.
Sort quickly directed Sinn to create a tunnel through the flames while the Malazans made their escape.
Nil
and
Nether
were shocked by Sinn's power, declaring her an unrealized
High Mage
in strength.
Unaware that any had survived, the 14th Army made haste for the
Kokakal Sea
to embark on
Admiral
Nok
's ships and escape the
Bluetongue Plague
ravaging Seven Cities. Sinn knew by instinct that a group of soldiers, including Shard, had survived the fires. She and Faradan Sort effectively deserted to stay behind as the 14th Army departed with Sinn hiding the pair from
Temul
's cavalry with her magic. Sort followed the uncommunicative girl without knowing specifically what she searched for in the ruins. After three days the pair discovered the place where Shard and the others had nearly tunneled out from beneath the city and helped them escape. Sinn crawled into her half-brother's arms and fell asleep.
Sinn and the others made the long march west, finally catching up to the army on the coast where she was greeted by
Grub
.
Sinn by
Corporal Nobbs
Aboard one of Nok's ships, Adjunct Tavore presented Sinn and Faradan Sort with the first badges bearing the new Bonehunters sigil designed by
T'amber
.
She became mute with all but her brother, who worried when she would not tell him what had happened to her at their former estate. When Sinn began intimately crawling under the cloaks of her fellow soldiers, he kept an eye on her, fearing someone might take advantage of her.  But when Shard found Sinn snuggled under
Masan Gilani
's cloak fondling and suckling her breasts, he did not feel moved to stop her.
Nok's fleet returned to
Malaz City
where the Adjunct met with Empress
Laseen
.
In
Reaper's Gale
Sinn by
Max Davenport
Adjunct Tavore clashed with Empress Laseen at Malaz City and took the
Bonehunters
rogue, following the
Tiste Edur
fleet
that had ravaged
Sepik
back to
Lether
to invade the
Letherii Empire
.
Cord and Balm's squads took the
Silanda
to the island of
Second Maiden Fort
off the coast of Lether to establish a headquarters and resupply base for the Adjunct.
They found the island on the verge of being destroyed under a mountain of ice released by the collapse of
Gothos
' ancient
Omtose Phellack
ritual, but Sinn was able to hold the ice back with her magic until its force was spent. The island's self-declared ruler,
Brullyg
, gratefully welcomed the Malazans as royal guests until they placed him under house arrest and secretly took control of the island.
While Balm's squad kept Brullyg under guard and monitored the island from its only town, Cord's squad patrolled the island's coast and interior while awaiting Tavore's arrival.
Sinn served as a go-between, able to transport herself instantly across the island in a swirl of light when one of the Malazans called her name. Brullyg was terrified of the "scrawny little mute girl."
She was equally feared by her own squad mates. Neither
Widdershins
nor
Ebron
had any idea how she fended off the
Jaghut
ice, and it delivered a bad jolt to Ebron's confidence in his own abilities. He said Sinn was not merely holding the ice back, but killing the Jaghut magic that fueled it by weaving its threads into something else.
Shard saw him make warding signs at Sinn's back whenever she came too close to the mage.
Limp was so frightened of Sinn that his bad knees knocked whenever she drew near.
Shard was sick with worry over his sister, who had stopped speaking to anyone including himself. The giggling girl he once carried over his shoulders was gone since Y'Ghatan and it frightened him. Now she was a child witch with straggly black hair, a
High Mage
with a thirst for blood, and a Child of
Dryjhna
the Apocalyptic.
She barely ever slept, but never looked tired,
and she made piping shrieks and played a bone flute as she cavorted about in a frenzy as if spider-bitten.
Bottle
thought her a natural talent, but completely insane.
Even
Pully
and
Skwish
, the
Shake
witches, were disturbed by her presence.
Only Masan Gilani still saw her as the girl who had once crawled into her arms when Cord argued she was just as much a High Mage as
Quick Ben
.
Meanwhile Tavore sent Fist Keneb's marines to the mainland, spreading them in isolated pairs of squads across thirty leagues of coast and burning their
transport vessels
behind them. The marines moved forward into the
Letherii
countryside towards
Letheras
, the capital, with orders to kill Edur by night and stir the occupied Letherii into rebellion. Each squad had a mage responsible for hiding their presence and confusing their enemies.
Shurq Elalle
and her ship,
Undying Gratitude
, were caught up in the Malazan blockade of Second Maiden Fort's port. When Adjunct Tavore arrived with the rest of the Malazan fleet, she hired the pirate to guide them to the mouth of the
Lether River
leading to Letheras.
The Adjunct's fleet made landfall near Letheras and Sinn was standing with Grub on the foredeck of the
Froth Wolf
when she gasped, feeling
Beak
's sacrifice to save Keneb's marines before the city walls.
While the Adjunct's forces defeated the city's
Imperial Brigade
,
Keneb's marines secretly entered the city to secure its western gate to allow the rest of the army entrance.
Sinn accompanied the Adjunct and her cavalry as they raced ahead to reinforce the gate's defence. Sinn seemed in a drunken daze as they approached the gate, but began laughing and clapping when she saw
Silchas Ruin
driven from the city by
Moranth munitions
and Quick Ben's magic. Soon the City Garrison surrendered and the city fell.
In
Dust of Dreams
Sinn by
Shadaan
She and Grub followed
Bent
and
Roach
into the dying
Azath house
in
Letheras
and disappeared into a Warren for a time, only to reappear at a crucial point in the battle between the
K'Chain Nah'ruk
and the
K'Chain Che'Malle
. She helped the Che'Malle win the battle by incinerating several Nah'ruk
Skykeeps
.
She initially used speech
but became more and more reticent until in the later books many assumed her to be either mute or dumb. She developed a very close friendship with Grub, the only person who knew that she was only mute by choice.
She was a natural High Mage, wielding the
warren
of
Telas
and ultimately was promoted to the rank of High Mage within the Bonehunters.
In
The Crippled God
Interpretation of Sinn by
Shadaan
Sinn was increasingly feared by those around her. The K'Chain Che'Malle
Assassin
Gu'Rull
even thought to kill her and Grub.
As time went on, her powers increased, but, at the same time, her grasp of reality and her allegiance to the Bonehunters waned. In her mind she relived her rape and mistreatment (as well as that of her family) which happened during the Seven Cities Rebellion. Obsessing about this fueled her rage and contributed to her becoming increasingly psychopathic. Her internal musings also revealed her complicity in the killing of
Keneb
, which was caused by her wanting to remove the
Fist
from Grub's life.
Ultimately, she turned against the Bonehunters and was killed by
Stormy
on the steps of the
Great Spire
.
Quotes
"
I am your fire, Grub, and I will burn to ash anything and anyone who dares gets close to you. That is why I rode the lizard's lightning, that brilliant fire. I rode it straight for Keneb.
"
―Sinn

sergeant

, from the same tribe as

.
She joined the army to follow her beloved sister,
as she always tried to keep her sister out of trouble.
Sinter was the subject of Badan Gruk's affection, and he had followed her into the army in an attempt to be with her.
Corporal
Pravalak Rim
of the 4th squad was infatuated with her sister, but when Kisswhere laughed off his attempts to woo her, Sinter privately urged him not to give up.

Corporal

, sapper

, sapper

Skanarow
was a
captain
in the
Bonehunters
. She was described as uncharacteristically tall and lean-limbed for a
Kanese
, with black hair. Her features were described as harsh and seamed in scars, but she was capable of a lovely smile.

described the look of her face as "if she's suckled among wildcats as a child".
According to
Kindly
, her name was archaic Kanese for a female hill-dog.
When she cited a saying amongst the old ones of her people, the idioms used seemed to indicate a descent from fishing folk.
In
Dust of Dreams
On the march to
Kolanse
she became involved with Ruthan Gudd, whom she suspected of living under a false name.

Skim
was a
sapper
in the
Bonehunters
'
8th Legion
, 3rd Company and part of
Badan Gruk
's 5th squad. She was one of several women who were the objects of
Honey
's unwanted affections, and regularly warned him to stop calling her "beloved".
Skim also complained that Badan Gruk's dark skin and love of moonless nights made him seem to disappear in the dark when his squad needed him the most.
In
Reaper's Gale
Adjunct
Tavore Paran
clashed with Empress
Laseen
at
Malaz City
and took the Bonehunters rogue, following the
Tiste Edur
fleet
that had ravaged
Sepik
back to
Lether
.
Tavore invaded the
Letherii Empire
, burning her
transport
vessels on the shoreline and spreading the
marines
in isolated pairs of squads across thirty leagues of coast. The marines moved forward into the
Letherii
countryside towards
Letheras
, the capital, with orders to kill Edur by night and stir the occupied Letherii into rebellion. Each squad had a mage responsible for hiding their presence and confusing their enemies.
Badan Gruk's squad, along with
Sinter
's 4th and
Primly
's 10th squads, landed furthest south of all the marines. Remaining together, they saw little resistance moving east and soon reached a river. Rather than slog through through waist-deep swamp muck, they stole a fisher boat and sailed upriver. They made excellent time until running into a Letherii galley in the night.
Kisswhere
and Sinter were lost in the water during a discharge of
Moranth munitions
. Forced ashore, they were pursued day and night, using up their mages dodging and ducking enemy attacks. On the first night, Badan Gruk lost his corporal after the man fell down an abandoned well shaft and broke his neck. Badan Gruk chose
Ruffle
to take his place. Somewhere along the way the
Heavy
,
Masker
, was also lost, but Badan Gruk,
Skulldeath
, and others had yet to draw blood.
Brushing off Honey's advances, Skim facetiously blamed him for Kisswhere's death, claiming Kisswhere had blown up her sister and herself to get away from him. Then she tormented
Nep Furrow
asking him to bless (or curse) her
sharpers
in the same manner he had done for Kisswhere before her death. Death was the only way Honey would leave her alone. Nep Furrow wanted nothing to do with the "teasin' tit-woman."
Contrary to the Adjunct's expectations, the Letherii soldiers did not use the
Malazan
invasion to turn against their Edur occupiers.
The marines further north saw intense action, and as they neared Letheras fighting became more desperate and their munition supplies dwindled.
Hellian
and
Urb
's squads earned the support of the Letherii slave and
Indebted
classes by changing tactics to slay the government officials, lawyers, and debt-holders in each village.
Fiddler
and
Gesler
's squads joined them at a tavern a day's travel from the capital just in time for a force of hundreds of Edur to envelop the village the Malazans occupied.
Three days after leaving the river, Badan Gruk, Sinter, and Primly's squads came upon the overwhelmed Malazans and turned the battle with their fresh supply of munitions. The new arrivals deferred to Fiddler's seniority, and the former
Bridgeburner
ordered the marines to hold their position in hopes they would be reinforced by
Fist
Keneb
.
Skim described Keneb's troops when they arrived as the ugliest faces you ever wanted to give a big wet kiss.
But thousands of Edur followed in Keneb's wake, pushing the gathered Malazans towards the city where the
Imperial Brigade
awaited.
Caught between the two armies near
Kravos Hill
, the 800 remaining Malazans
were forced to huddle under
Beak
's protective spell when the Letherii mages cast a deadly
ritual
of
Chaos
upon them and the Edur. The spell was broken, but the hair of all those under Beak's protection turned white. The Edur abandoned the field after their allies' betrayal, and the shaken Imperial Brigade withdrew to meet Adjunct Tavore's more threatening main force as it disembarked from the
Lether River
.
Keneb marched on Letheras thinking the marines deserved to be the first to enter the capital.
After the marines found a hidden entrance beneath the wall, Badan Gruk's squad was among those sent to secure the city's western gate from the inside to allow the main army entrance into the city. City Garrison soldiers tried to retake the gate in bloody fighting, but Badan Gruk's squad held on long enough for to greet Adjunct Tavore and her group of cavalry when they arrived.
Soon the City Garrison surrendered and the city fell.
In
Dust of Dreams
(Information needed)
In
The Crippled God
It was revealed that Skim had died, presumably in the battle against the
K'Chain Nah'ruk
.

Skulldeath
Biographical information
Pseudonyms
Tribole Futan
Race
Human
(
Gilani
)
Gender
Male
Social information
Affiliation
Malazan Empire
Malazan 14th Army
Bonehunters
Occupation(s)
Marine
Skulldeath
, formerly
Tribole Futan
, was the last surviving male of the Futani royal line of the
Gilani
tribe of southeast
Seven Cities
. He was a 23-year-old
marine
in
Primly
's 10th Squad,
8th Legion
, 3rd Company, of the
Bonehunters
. Skulldeath was not tall, but very strong as his physique was pure muscle and devoid of all fat. He had dark, almond-shaped eyes which were considered to be quite feminine.
He was not outspoken and his rare smiles were as shy as a young maiden's.
Skulldeath fought in the Gilani style with two giant tulwars which had once belonged to his great-uncle, a
Falah'dan
champion. He performed patterns like the "lishgar efhanah", the leaping attack, or the Edged Net as it was also called — a specific jumping mid-air attack against the enemies' heads, which killed them instantly.
Skulldeath was considered very attractive by both genders and did not have any concerns about indulging in same sex relations, as he did not consider these liaisons to be infringing on his vow to save the last of the Futani seed for a queen or empress as befitted his royal station. Dalliances in which men used him were harmless and pleasurable and "such was his discipline that he had not spilled seed once, not even in his sleep".
He was given the name Skulldeath by
Master Sergeant
Braven Tooth
in
Malaz City
, who was known for his apt naming of recruits.
The name was likely based on Skulldeath's fighting style with which the Sergeant would have been familiar.
Bottle
and
Koryk
speculated that the name might have been a reference to the
Skulldeath plant
, found on
Malaz Island
. The plant had only male specimens, but was still able to produce by spreading pollen which infected the seeds of other plants.
Mulvan Dreader
linked the name to Skulldeath's sexual discipline, calling the young soldier "truly a man about to explode."
In
Reaper's Gale
Adjunct
Tavore Paran
clashed with Empress
Laseen
at
Malaz City
and took the Bonehunters rogue, following the
Tiste Edur
fleet
that had ravaged
Sepik
back to
Lether
.
Tavore invaded the
Letherii Empire
, burning her
transport
vessels on the shoreline and spreading the
marines
in isolated pairs of squads across thirty leagues of coast. The marines moved forward into the
Letherii
countryside towards
Letheras
, the capital, with orders to kill Edur by night and stir the occupied Letherii into rebellion. Each squad had a mage responsible for hiding their presence and confusing their enemies.
Primly's squad, along with
Sinter
's 4th and
Badan Gruk
's 5th squads, landed furthest south of all the marines. Remaining together, they saw little resistance moving east and soon reached a river. Rather than slog through through waist-deep swamp muck, they stole a fisher boat and sailed upriver. They made excellent time until running into a Letherii galley in the night.
Kisswhere
and Sinter were lost in the water during a discharge of
Moranth munitions
. Forced ashore, they were pursued day and night, using up their mages dodging and ducking enemy attacks. Somewhere along the way
Masker
was also lost, leaving Primly with only one heavy. Despite this action, Skulldeath, Badan Gruk and others had yet to draw blood.
Contrary to the Adjunct's expectations, the Letherii soldiers did not use the
Malazan
invasion to turn against their Edur occupiers.
The marines further north saw intense action, and as they neared Letheras fighting became more desperate and their munition supplies dwindled.
Hellian
and
Urb
's squads earned the support of the Letherii slave and
Indebted
classes by changing tactics to slay the government officials, lawyers, and debt-holders in each village.
Fiddler
and
Gesler
's squads joined them at a tavern a day's travel from the capital just in time for a force of hundreds of Edur to envelop the village the Malazans occupied.
Skulldeath by
Dejan Delic
Three days after leaving the river, Primly, Badan Gruk, Sinter's squads came upon the overwhelmed Malazans and turned the battle with their fresh supply of munitions.
Skulldeath used his leaping fighting style to kill seven Tiste Edur who had cornered
Smiles
and Koryk in an alley, leaving the pair speechless.
The newly arriving squads deferred to Fiddler's seniority, and the former
Bridgeburner
ordered the marines to hold their position in hopes they would be reinforced by
Fist
Keneb
.
Intrigued by the handsome soldier, Smiles fruitlessly procured some Skulldeath plant from Bottle in the hopes of luring Skulldeath into a romantic liaison.
But ultimately it was Hellian who caught Skulldeath's attention when he overheard her drunkenly boast that she was the Queen of
Kartool
.
From then on he was besotted with her, announcing he had given his heart to her and following her everywhere.
Hellian returned the favour, forcing Primly to step in and pry them apart.
By the time Keneb's forces arrived, thousands of Edur followed in their wake, pushing the gathered Malazans towards the city where the
Imperial Brigade
awaited.
Caught between the two armies near
Kravos Hill
, the 800 remaining Malazans
were forced to huddle under
Beak
's protective spell when the Letherii mages cast a deadly
ritual
of
Chaos
upon them and the Edur. The spell was broken, but the hair of all those under Beak's protection turned white. The Edur abandoned the field after their allies' betrayal, and the shaken Imperial Brigade withdrew to meet Adjunct Tavore's more threatening main force as it disembarked from the
Lether River
.
Keneb marched on Letheras thinking the marines deserved to be the first to enter the capital.
After the marines found a hidden entrance beneath the wall, the seized the city's western gate to allow the rest of the army entrance.
Soon the City Garrison surrendered and the city fell.
In
Dust of Dreams
(Information needed)
In
The Crippled God
Skulldeath was in the final battle to defend the
Crippled God
. While fighting the
Kolanse
army, he died taking on multiple enemies, surrounded. A blow hammered him from behind, a hard edge crunching and grinding into his spine, before everything went dark.

PAGE: Smiles
CATEGORIES: Bonehunters
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Smiles
======================================================================

Smiles
Biographical information
Race
Human
(
Kanese
)
Gender
Female
Social information
Affiliation
Malazan Empire
Malaz 14th Army
Bonehunters
Occupation(s)
Marine
Smiles
was a young, female
Marine
in
Fiddler
's 4th Squad, 9th Company,
8th Legion
of the
Malaz 14th Army
. The name 'Smiles' itself was a pseudonym given to her by
Master Sergeant Braven Tooth
due to her disinclination to smile.
Fiddler thought the remorseless chill of her eyes reminded him of
Sorry
, and he wondered whether there was murder in her past.
She had petite features.
She preferred attacking from stealth and was rather skilled with the two thin-bladed knives she kept on her belt.
Smiles frequently came into conflict with her fellow squad member,
Koryk
.
In
House of Chains
Smiles journeyed to
Aren
as part of
Adjunct
Tavore Paran
's army to retake
Seven Cities
after the
Whirlwind
rebellion.
Fiddler designated Smiles and
Bottle
as the squad's scouts during the evening hours.
In
The Bonehunters
Smiles was one of the group of soldiers who survived the
Last Siege of Y'Ghatan
by tunneling their way out from under the city after it was burned by
Leoman of the Flails
.
In
Reaper's Gale
Smiles by
Dejan Delic
Later on during the
Letheras
invasion Smiles showed admiration and sexual interest towards Koryk due to his battle abilities.
In
Dust of Dreams
(Information needed)
In
The Crippled God
Shortnose
thought of her as a 'pretty little woman'.
Smiles began distancing herself from Koryk.
History
Smiles was born on an estate near a small village by the seashore in
Itko Kan
. When the sea stopped providing a catch for the local fisherfolk, the hungry villagers resorted to old blood rituals.  Smiles' twin sister was chosen by the elders to be sacrificed to the
Elder God
,
Mael
, because of the power inherent in a Mirror Birth. Her sister was drugged insensate with
Durhang
and left at the water's edge, bound and weighted down for the incoming tide and hungry crabs. Cursing the priests and villagers, Smiles fled to the great city to the north.
Quotes
Smiles
: "
...We're going to kill her, you know.
"
Bottle
: "
Really. Well, I won't shed any tears. Who is this “we” anyway?
"
Smiles
: "
Me and Cuttle. He'll distract her, I'll stick a knife in her back. Tonight.
"
Bottle
: "
Fist Keneb will have you strung up, you know.
"
Smiles
: "
We'll make it look like an accident.
"
―Smiles and Bottle talking about their new captain, Faradan Sort

======================================================================
PAGE: Sobelone
CATEGORIES: Bonehunters
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Sobelone
======================================================================

Sobelone
was a
Sergeant
in the
Heavy infantry
,
9th Company, 8th Legion
of the
Malaz 14th Army
. She was a typical mixed breed from
Malaz City
. Sobelone was a severe-looking woman with streaks of grey in her shoulder-length black hair, and eyes the colour of the sky.
She was older than her fellow sergeants in the Heavies,
Mosel
and
Tugg
, but Tugg was the biggest.
The three had a threatening air about them that had less to do with size than attitude, and were similar enough in look that they could almost be siblings.
Named Squad Members
Hanno
Toles
In
House of Chains
Sobelone's squad was part of
Adjunct
Tavore Paran
's punitive expedition against the
Army of the Apocalypse
.  There had been a restructuring of the 8th Legion and soon after the army arrived at
Raraku
, several of the sergeants from those squads who would join the
Marines
of 9th Company dropped in on
Strings
to introduce themselves. Amongst them were Sobelone and her fellow sergeants, Mosel and Tugg. Sobelone did not speak during the meeting.
Moak
, sergeant of the 11th squad, seemed to 'know things' but supposedly only shared his speculations with Tugg and Sobelone.
In
The Bonehunters
After the
Battle of Raraku
,
Leoman
led the Army of the Apocalypse westward to
Y'Ghatan
and the 14th Army followed.  Once the 14th Army reached the city's outskirts, an impromptu wrestling match broke out between
Saltlick
and
Shortnose
after Saltlick bit Shortnose's ear off. The rest of Sobelone and Tugg's squads gathered around the two straining men, watching and placing bets.
Adjunct Tavore launched the
Last Siege of Y'Ghatan
by sending the army's
sappers
to breach the city's wall under the cover of night. First into the city were the Malazan
marines
, followed quickly by the heavy and
medium infantry
.  Once inside the city, the Malazans immediately came under attack from hidden archers and warriors. Sobelone and
Toles
were killed in one such ambush.

======================================================================
PAGE: Squint
CATEGORIES: Bonehunters
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Squint
======================================================================

Squint
Biographical information
Race
Human
Gender
Male
Social information
Affiliation
Malazan Empire
Aren Guard
Malaz 14th Army
Occupation(s)
Soldier
"
Before the day's through, you bastard, ten thousand soldiers will be voicing your name.
"
―Commander
Blistig
, to Squint
Squint
was an old soldier in the
Aren Guard
.
He was a bowman,
and known as an expert marksman in
Aren
.
Squint was short and squat with forearms muscled like hemp ropes, and his eyes were like small, black marbles nested in wrinkles.
His head was bald but for a fringe of long, grey, ratty strands.
His uniform appeared not to have been washed or repaired in decades.
His longbow was as tall as he was.
In
Deadhouse Gates
Click here
to reveal section for
Deadhouse Gates
.
Squint was given the unenviable task of killing
Coltaine
to ease his suffering after the
Chain of Dogs
was massacred outside the city gates and the
Fist
himself crucified.  With a single shot, the weeping bowman struck Coltaine in the forehead at a distance of 500 paces.  Without this act of mercy, Coltaine's soul would not have been retrieved by the swarms of crows that descended onto the battlefield.
Enemy commander
Korbolo Dom
personally called for the bowman's death, but Squint had already disappeared.
Interpretation of Squint by
Enaglio
In
House of Chains
Squint was deeply affected by his role in Coltaine's death and retreated into alcoholism.  He had to be dragged from a bar and forcibly incorporated into
Adjunct
Tavore
's
14th Army
by Blistig and his men.
At the
Battle of Raraku
, Squint was now an officer in Blistig's
9th Legion
.  He was part of a small squad guarding the Adjunct, when
Karsa Orlong
rode onto the field on his
Jhag horse
.  Squint immediately recognised Karsa as a
Thelomen Toblakai
.
In
The Bonehunters
After the
Last Siege of Y'Ghatan
,
Admiral
Nok
and the Malazan Imperial Fleet extracted the 14th Army to return home to
Quon Tali
. Squint remained with the Adjunct's entourage aboard her flagship, the
Froth Wolf
.  The night after the battle between the Malazan fleet and the
Third Edur Imperial Fleet
,
Apsalar
found him at the ship's rail looking into the night.  Squint at first refused to introduce himself, claiming knowledge of his identity would only end their conversation with awkward silence.  When he finally relented he was pleased when Apsalar, an outsider to the army, professed not to know his history.
The archer and the assassin shared their burdens of pain and Squint counseled her not to give up her love for
Crokus
. They agreed to meet for similar conversations in the future. Afterwards, Apsalar's thoughts revealed that she had known his identity all along and that the archer was the only one in the army who could not forgive himself for taking Coltaine's life.

PAGE: Stacker
CATEGORIES: Bonehunters
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Stacker
======================================================================

Stacker
was a
Corporal
in
Sergeant
Moak
's 11th
Medium infantry
squad in the
8th Legion
of the
Malaz 14th Army
.
In
House of Chains
Stacker was part of
Adjunct
Tavore Paran
's punitive expedition against the
Army of the Apocalypse
.  On the road from
Aren
to
Raraku
, he, Moak, and
Burnt
had done their share of the fighting, and their names were well known amongst the other soldiers in the legion.
In
The Bonehunters
After the
Battle of Raraku
,
Leoman
led the Army of the Apocalypse westward to
Y'Ghatan
and the 14th Army followed. Upon reaching the outskirts of the city, Moak prepared a stew for his squad using a ripened fish he had carried for weeks.  When his squad all "got the squats", he blamed it on their weak stomachs while a true soldier like himself suffered only from belches that smelled of rotting fish guts.
In the hours before the
Last Siege of Y'Ghatan
, Moak engaged Sergeant
Balm
in a game of
Troughs
, but Balm soon became disoriented, unclear who he was and what he was doing.  Balm's corporal,
Deadsmell
, led him to safety from an angry Moak, who claimed Balm had cursed him and his squad since Moak had been winning.  Stacker calmed his sergeant by identifying Balm's malady as "the Confusion", a condition developed by some just before battle.
Adjunct
Tavore Paran
launched the attack on Y'Ghatan by sending the army's
sappers
to breach the city's wall under the cover of night. First into the city were the Malazan
marines
, followed quickly by the
heavy
and medium infantry. Barely a street in and fearing an ambush, Sergeant
Gesler
called up Moak's squad as well as
Thom Tissy
's sappers and
Tugg
's heavies to clear the surrounding buildings. In the fighting that followed, the poorly trained sappers misfired their
munitions
. One shrieking sapper exited the building fully aflame.  As Moak's squad went to help him, the sapper's munitions satchel went off killing Stacker and Moak's entire squad.

PAGE: Strap Mull
CATEGORIES: Bonehunters
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Strap_Mull

Strap Mull
was a
Dal Honese
sapper
in the 4th squad,
8th Legion
, 3rd Company of the
Bonehunters
.
In
Reaper's Gale
Adjunct
Tavore Paran
clashed with Empress
Laseen
at
Malaz City
and took the Bonehunters rogue, following the
Tiste Edur
fleet
that had ravaged
Sepik
back to
Lether
.
Tavore invaded the
Letherii Empire
, burning her
transport
vessels on the shoreline and spreading the
marines
in isolated pairs of squads across thirty leagues of coast. The marines moved forward into the
Letherii
countryside towards
Letheras
, the capital, with orders to kill Edur by night and stir the occupied Letherii into rebellion. Each squad had a mage responsible for hiding their presence and confusing their enemies.
Sinter's squad, along with
Badan Gruk
's 5th and
Primly
's 10th squads, landed furthest south of all the marines. Remaining together, they saw little resistance moving east and soon reached a river. Rather than slog through through waist-deep swamp muck, they stole a fisher boat and sailed upriver. They made excellent time until running into a Letherii galley in the night.
Kisswhere
and Sinter were lost in the water during a discharge of
Moranth munitions
. Forced ashore, they were pursued day and night, using up their mages dodging and ducking enemy attacks.
Corporal
Pravalak Rim
led the 4th squad in Sinter's place.
Strap Mull was friendly with his fellow Dal Hon,
Neller
, from the 10th squad. After Kisswhere's death, the two spoke in their native language about Corporal Rim's despair over the woman he had been infatuated with. Neller also wondered if the fighting in Letheras would be anything like
Y'ghatan
, where their squad had done nothing. Strap Mull told him to stop worrying until they got there. Neller carried a sword that Strap Mull had found in a Letherii cabin, but given away once he realised it howled like a wild woman every time it hit something. The sound bothered Strap Mull enough that he stopped his ears with moss whenever he knew Neller planned to use it.
Contrary to the Adjunct's expectations, the Letherii soldiers did not use the
Malazan
invasion to turn against their Edur occupiers.
The marines further north saw intense action, and as they neared Letheras fighting became more desperate and their munition supplies dwindled.
Hellian
and
Urb
's squads earned the support of the Letherii slave and
Indebted
classes by changing tactics to slay the government officials, lawyers, and debt-holders in each village.
Fiddler
and
Gesler
's squads joined them at a tavern a day's travel from the capital just in time for a force of hundreds of Edur to envelop the village the Malazans occupied.
Three days after leaving the river, Sinter, Primly, and Badan Gruk's squads came upon the overwhelmed Malazans and turned the tide of battle with their fresh supply of munitions. The new arrivals deferred to Fiddler's seniority, and the former
Bridgeburner
ordered the marines to hold their position in hopes they would be reinforced by
Fist
Keneb
.
Noting Gesler and
Stormy
among the village's marines, Lookback argued with Drawfirst and Shoaly over whether the pair should be killed for betraying the
Cult of the Boar
. Shoaly argued that Gesler and Stormy were not to blame for the cult being outlawed and asked Drawfirst to "explain it to this fool." Drawfirst said they were all going to die in the coming engagement and Lookback had the choice of dying with his fellow heavies or dying alone. If she saw him creeping up on Gesler or Stormy she would lop his head off herself.
By the time Keneb's forces arrived, thousands of Edur followed in their wake, pushing the gathered Malazans towards the city where the
Imperial Brigade
awaited.
Caught between the two armies near
Kravos Hill
, the 800 remaining Malazans
were forced to huddle under
Beak
's protective spell when the Letherii mages cast a deadly
ritual
of
Chaos
upon them and the Edur. The spell was broken, but the hair of all those under Beak's protection turned white. The Edur abandoned the field after their allies' betrayal, and the shaken Imperial Brigade withdrew to meet Adjunct Tavore's more threatening main force as it disembarked from the
Lether River
.
Keneb marched on Letheras thinking the marines deserved to be the first to enter the capital.
After the marines found a hidden entrance beneath the wall, the seized the city's western gate to allow the rest of the army entrance.
Soon the City Garrison surrendered and the city fell.
In
Dust of Dreams
(Information needed)
In
The Crippled God
It was revealed Strap Mull had died earlier, presumably during the battle against the
K'Chain Nah'ruk
.

======================================================================
PAGE: Sunrise
CATEGORIES: Bonehunters
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Sunrise
======================================================================

Sunrise
was a former
Letherii
craftsman and a member of
Hedge's
New Bridgeburners
.
He was a scrawny man who looked about forty years old, with a huge stained moustache.
In
Dust of Dreams
Originally the man who would be named Sunrise had been a craftsman in
Letheras
, who made lamps from bronze, copper and glazed clay, and sold them to the temples. His business was doing well, so he invested into the building trade. When
Tehol Beddict
destroyed the Letherii economy, he lost all of his wealth and his wife left him, revealing that she had only been waiting to find someone richer than him. He contemplated suicide, but instead decided to join the
Bonehunters
as a recruit, to leave Letheras behind.
Master Sergeant Pores
was tasked by
Captain Kindly
with taking care of the new recruits. He made the former craftsman an acting sergeant but also named him
Twit
, before handing the recruits off to the sergeants
Badan Gruk
,
Sinter
and
Primly
.
Twit wasn't too happy about his new name and the treatment by Pores. He talked to
Ruffle
about it and she suggested that he should just change his name. While listening to his story she came up with the name
Sunrise
. Sunrise liked the idea and adopted the name.
Later Sunrise and his fellow thirty-nine recruits were snatched up by
Bavedict
to join
Hedge's
New Bridgeburners
. Sunrise and
Nose Stream
were the first sergeants of the new unit, with
Rumjugs
and
Sweetlard
as their corporals.
Sunrise came to really enjoyed his time with Hedge and his new comrades, with all the freedom and camraderie. He was very proud of being part of a continuation of a famous Malazan company and was eager to prove himself.
During the battle against the
K'Chain Nah'ruk
, Sunrise was killed by the Nah'ruk lightning nodes as he pushed Hedge out of the line of fire.
Quotes
"
And then there were the wonderful beasts in those distant lands. Dragonflies big enough to ride— imagine whizzing through the clouds, looking down on everything! Seeing how beautiful it all was, and then dropping hundreds of bombs on it.
"
―Sunrise daydreaming about being a Bridgeburner

======================================================================
PAGE: T'amber
CATEGORIES: Bonehunters
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/T'amber
======================================================================

T'amber
Biographical information
Race
Human
Gender
Female
Social information
Affiliation
Malazan Empire
Bonehunters
T'amber
[TAM-ber]
was
Adjunct
Tavore Paran
's aide and rumoured lover.
She was not very talkative and was described as beautiful and remote.
Her origins were unclear. Her name apparently came from her "tawny mane"
or her eyes, which had the colour of amber.
She dressed in hard leathers and carried a long sword.
In
Deadhouse Gates
T'amber was by Tavore's side when the nobles chosen for
The Cull
in
Unta
were led from
Judgment's Round
to the slave ships outside the city.  Amongst the slaves was
Felisin Paran
, Tavore's sister.
She later accompanied the Adjunct and the
Malaz 14th Army
to
Aren
on
Seven Cities
as part of the punitive expedition against the
Whirlwind
uprising.
In
House of Chains
T'amber by
Dejan Delic
T'amber was confirmed as Tavore's lover. According to
Gamet
she had been a concubine in the Grand Temple of the
Queen of Dreams
in Unta.
She accompanied Tavore as the Malaz 14th Army marched from Aren to
Raraku
, staying in a modest tent near the Adjunct's own.
She apparently conducted morning sword practice with the Adjunct.
When
Sha'ik Reborn
challenged Tavore to a personal duel at the
Battle of Raraku
, Captain
Keneb
went to find T'amber to see if she would assist Tavore in donning her armour.  T'amber declined, saying her help was not needed.
In
The Bonehunters
'Flight from Malaz City' by
Corporal Nobbs
After the
Battle of Raraku
,
Leoman
led the
Army of the Apocalypse
westward to
Y'Ghatan
and the 14th Army followed. T'amber continued to serve Tavore, but she was not held in respect by any of the Fists at the Adjunct's command.
During the
Last Siege of Y'Ghatan
, she observed the battle at Tavore's side along with
Nil
and
Nether
.
It was revealed that the decorations Tavore awarded to
Faradan Sort
and
Sinn
were crafted by T'amber. Her family had been jewelsmiths and she herself had been an apprentice. To Bottle her talent was like genius.
Along with
Kalam Mekhar
, T'amber helped Adjunct Paran escape the
Claw
agents sent to kill Tavore before she could escape
Malaz City
. After Kalam sent T'amber and Tavore on ahead of him, trying to buy them some time, T'amber was impaled and killed on the docks just before the sapper
Fiddler
reached the Adjunct.  Fiddler dragged Tavore on to the jetty where the
Froth Wolf
was moored, helping her finally escape the trap set for her by Empress
Laseen
.
Afterwards, it was revealed that T'amber's body was inhabited by the
Elder Goddess
, the
Eres'al
, as witnessed by
Grub
and
Lostara Yil
. Grub told Lostara Yil that she must not tell Tavore that the Eres'al used T'amber's body.
Earlier on in the voyage, Tavore made a reference to T'amber being a lot more now than she once was, possibly indicating that Tavore was not as unaware as Grub believed.
In
Reaper's Gale
T'amber and Tavore by
Dorian Sesar
Tavore was stricken with grief by T'amber's death, although she tried to remain in tight control of her emotions so that it did not show. But
Blistig
,
Withal
, and the others aboard the
Froth Wolf
recognised her as a woman more dead than alive. By the time the fleet neared
Theft
to resupply, the 14th Army was demoralised and near mutiny with no home to return to. Lostara Yil stepped in to replace T'amber as Tavore's personal aide to manage the nearly eight thousand remaining miserable soldiers. She reawakened the Adjunct's spirit in a night-long argument in the Adjunct's cabin. Afterwards, Tavore called together the Fists and senior officers to deliver a
speech
defining the Bonehunters within the context of other storied Malazan armies and steeling them for the fight ahead. Despite being cast off by the Empress, they were still Malazan and Tavore held onto the title of Adjunct. It was at this point that the first hints of her plans were revealed and she finished her speech with T'amber's words: "What awaits you in the dusk of the old world's passing, shall go...unwitnessed."
Despite Tavore's evident grief, there still existed suspicion about the events at Malaz City among some members of the Bonehunters. Even Keneb pondered whether Tavore and the Empress had planned yet another Malazan army "gone rogue", but he concluded the Adjunct would never have agreed to T'amber's murder.
Throatslitter
put some of the blame of T'amber's death on Withal, the man the Bonehunters went to Malaz City to get.
Trivia
According to author
Steven Erikson
, T'amber's connection to the Eres'al did not develop until after
Deadhouse Gates
.
"I don't know if I had in mind that T'amber is in anyway possessed. Eres'al, in a sense, stays both inside and outside the individuals she puts her attention towards...I didn't think of her as being constantly on T'amber's shoulder, but the fact that T'amber and Tavore were mates, were lovers, or in love with each other is a thematic embodiment of the Eres'al anyways...For the journey through Malaz City, that is an instance of the most direct connection that the Eres'al makes with T'amber, employing T'amber's love for Tavore because that is what drives T'amber to defend Tavore the entire journey."

======================================================================
PAGE: Taffo
CATEGORIES: Bonehunters
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Taffo
======================================================================

Taffo
was a
sapper
in the 9th Company,
8th Legion
of the
Malaz 14th Army
in
Sergeant
Mosel
's
Heavy infantry
squad.
In
The Bonehunters
After the
Battle of Raraku
,
Leoman
led the
Army of the Apocalypse
westward to
Y'Ghatan
and the 14th Army followed.  Once the 14th Army reached the city's outskirts, Mosel and his squad decided to take revenge on the wagon whose dust they had eaten over many long miles. They bound and gagged the wagoner and the load crew in the long grass before proceeding to pry the wagon apart. Under Mosel's watchful eye,
Flashwit
and
Mayfly
pried the nails, studs, and fittings from the wagon's boards while Taffo and
Uru Hela
struggled with an axle.
Adjunct
Tavore Paran
launched the
Last Siege of Y'Ghatan
by sending the army's sappers to breach the city's wall under the cover of night. The sappers were organised into groups with each group protected by a
mage
.  Taffo's group included
Able
,
Bowl
,
Gupp
, and
Jump
with
Balgrid
as their mage.
Once the walls were breached Taffo quickly returned to Mosel's squad of
Heavy infantry
.
First into the city were the Malazan
marines
, followed quickly by the heavies.  The marines were immediately ambushed by swordsmen on the ground and archers in the buildings above them.  Mosel's squad of heavies waded into the swordsmen just as
Fiddler
launched a
cusser
from his
Crossbow
into the windows of the building above them.  The resulting explosion crushed Taffo under a heap of rubble. An angry Mosel descended on Fiddler before the continued fighting pulled him away.

======================================================================
PAGE: Tarr
CATEGORIES: Bonehunters
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Tarr
======================================================================

Tarr
Biographical information
Race
Human
(
Hengan
)
Gender
Male
Social information
Affiliation
Malazan Empire
Malaz 14th Army
Bonehunters
Occupation(s)
Marine
Rank
Corporal
Corporal
Tarr
was a
marine
in
Sergeant
Strings
' 4th Squad in the
Malaz 14th Army
. He was a nondescript
Hengan
, with pale, stolid features and placid, pallid eyes.
He rarely spoke and was slow to act without orders, attributes Strings felt beneficial in a corporal.
He was known for his unyielding stance with a shield. It was said that once during training, Master Sergeant
Braven Tooth
had spent nearly two bells pounding on him with a mace but was unable to get past the shield. His ability to remain unbudged once he planted his feet led the Master Sergeant to give him the name, "Tarr", as if his feet were stuck fast to the ground.
Tarr liked the idea of being unmovable and saw his role in the squad as being first to the front, giving the others time to bring whatever they had to bear.
Braven Tooth was convinced to place Tarr in the marines rather than the
Heavy infantry
based on his skill with a
crossbow
.
Tarr designed his gear to allow him immediate action in combat. Rather than keep his oversized shield on his back like most soldiers, he carried it strapped to his left hand.
His equipment pack had quick-release clasps that allowed him to shed it with one hand, while the other reached for his short thick-bladed sword.
His scaled iron hauberk provided a satisfying anchoring weight.
He spoke with a recognisable Hengan accent.
In
House of Chains
Tarr was part of
Adjunct
Tavore Paran
's punitive expedition against the
Army of the Apocalypse
.  Strings immediately promoted him to corporal upon their arrival in
Aren
.
On the road to
Raraku
, he was the Trainer for
Joyful Union
, the 4th squad's entrant in the 9th Company
Scorpion
fight.
In
The Bonehunters
Tarr was one of the group of soldiers who survived the
Last Siege of Y'Ghatan
by escaping through tunneling their way out from under the city.
In
Reaper's Gale
Interpretation of Corabb and Tarr by
Slaine69
Tarr thought that
Corabb
was trying to prove himself and outdo Tarr whereas in reality, Corabb stuck close to the corporal to protect the man's weak side even though it meant disobeying Fiddler's order of guarding Bottle.
In
Dust of Dreams
(Information needed)
In
The Crippled God
After Fiddler's promotion to Captain, Tarr took over as Sergeant. He promoted Corabb to be his Corporal. Tarr was described as having a greying beard.
